2:24:1397:0:14:72:519:700:12:Times:12:Times:Credit Market Shocks and Economic Fluctuations: Evidence from Corporate Bond and Stock
2:25:1482:14:14:72:111:686:12:Times:12:Times:Markets
2:26:1489:14:14:72:341:672:12:Times:12:Times:Simon Gilchrist, Vladimir Yankov, and Egon Zakrajsek
2:27:1541:14:14:72:234:658:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 14863
2:28:1569:14:14:72:124:644:12:Times:12:Times:April 2009
2:29:1579:14:28:72:180:630:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. E32,E44,G12
2:30:1598:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:31:1606:28:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:To identify disruptions in credit markets, research on the role of asset prices in economic fluctuations
2:32:1710:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:has focused on the information content of various corporate credit spreads. We re-examine this evidence
2:33:1813:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:using a broad array of credit spreads constructed directly from the secondary bond prices on outstanding
2:34:1917:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:senior unsecured debt issued by a large panel of nonfinancial firms. An advantage of our "ground-up''
2:35:2018:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:approach is that we are able to construct matched portfolios of equity returns, which allows us to examine
2:36:2124:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:the information content of bond spreads that is orthogonal to the information contained in stock prices
2:37:2227:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:of the same set of firms, as well as in macroeconomic variables measuring economic activity, inflation,
2:38:2330:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:interest rates, and other financial indicators. Our portfolio-based bond spreads contain substantial predictive
2:39:2441:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:power for economic activity and outperform—especially at longer horizons—standard default-risk
2:40:2535:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:indicators. Much of the predictive power of bond spreads for economic activity is embedded in securities
2:41:2639:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:issued by intermediate-risk rather than high-risk firms. According to impulse responses from a structural
2:42:2744:14:14:72:540:420:12:Times:12:Times:factor-augmented vector autoregression, unexpected increases in bond spreads cause large and persistent
2:43:2847:14:14:72:540:406:12:Times:12:Times:contractions in economic activity. Indeed, shocks emanating from the corporate bond market account
2:44:2945:14:14:72:539:392:12:Times:12:Times:for more than 30 percent of the forecast error variance in economic activity at the two- to four-year
2:45:3045:14:14:72:540:378:12:Times:12:Times:horizon. Overall, our results imply that credit market shocks have contributed significantly to U.S.
2:46:3145:14:42:72:324:364:12:Times:12:Times:economic fluctuations during the 1990–2008 period.
2:47:3195:42:14:72:148:322:12:Times:12:Times:Simon Gilchrist
2:48:3210:14:14:72:198:308:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:49:3233:14:14:72:160:294:12:Times:12:Times:Boston University
2:50:3250:14:14:72:168:280:12:Times:12:Times:270 Bay State Road
2:51:3268:14:14:72:167:266:12:Times:12:Times:Boston, MA  02215
2:52:3285:14:14:72:124:252:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:53:3293:14:28:72:151:238:12:Times:12:Times:sgilchri@bu.edu
2:54:3308:28:14:72:156:210:12:Times:12:Times:Vladimir Yankov

2:62:3453:14:14:306:416:294:12:Times:12:Times:Federal Reserve Board
2:63:3474:14:14:306:499:280:12:Times:12:Times:20th Street & Constitution Avenue, NW
2:64:3511:14:14:306:426:266:12:Times:12:Times:Washington, D.C. 20551

3:66:3555:0:28:90:203:692:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:1  Introduction
3:67:3570:28:16:90:521:664:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:After markets for securitized credit products collapsed dramatically in the second half of
3:68:3660:16:17:90:522:648:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2007, growth in a number of industrialized economies slowedmarkedly, suggesting that
3:69:3744:17:16:90:521:631:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:disruptions in financial markets can have important macroeconomic consequences.  The
3:70:3828:16:16:90:522:615:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:fact that sharp and sudden deteriorations in financial conditions are typically followed by
3:71:3919:16:17:90:522:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a prolonged period of economic weakness is a feature of a growing number of economic
3:72:4003:17:16:90:521:582:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:downturns in the U.S. and abroad.  During periods of credit market turmoil, financial
3:73:4088:16:17:90:522:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:asset prices, owing to their forward-looking nature, are especially informative of linkages
3:74:4179:17:16:90:521:549:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between the real and financial sides of economy: Movements inasset prices can provide
3:75:4264:16:17:90:521:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:early-warning signals for such economic downturns and can beused to gauge the degree of
3:76:4351:17:16:90:222:516:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:strains in financial markets.
3:77:4380:16:16:106:521:500:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Past research on the role of asset prices in signaling futureeconomic conditions and
3:78:4464:16:17:89:521:484:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in propagating economic fluctuations has emphasized the information content of default-
3:79:4551:17:16:89:521:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk indicators such as corporate credit spreads—the difference in yields between various
3:80:4640:16:17:89:522:451:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:corporate debt instruments and government securities of comparable maturity—for the state
3:81:4729:17:16:89:522:434:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the economy and risks to the economic outlook.1In a recent paper, Philippon [2008]
3:82:4814:16:17:89:521:418:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:provides a theoretical framework in which the predictive content of corporate bond spreads
3:83:4904:17:16:89:522:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for economic activity—absent any financial frictions—reflects a general decline in economic
3:84:4995:16:17:89:522:385:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:fundamentals stemming from a reduction in the expected present value of corporate cash
3:85:5081:17:16:89:521:368:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:flows prior to a cyclical downturn. Rising credit spreads canalso reflect disruptions in the
3:86:5173:16:16:89:522:352:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:supply of credit resulting from the worsening in the qualityof corporate balance sheets
3:87:5260:16:17:89:522:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:or from the deterioration in the health of financial intermediaries that supply credit—the
3:88:5350:17:16:89:522:319:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:financial accelerator mechanism emphasized by Bernanke, Gertler, and Gilchrist [1999]. In
3:89:5439:16:17:89:521:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this context, a contraction in credit supply causes asset values to fall, incentives to default to
3:90:5537:17:16:89:521:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increase, and yield spreads on private debt instruments to widen before economic downturns,
3:91:5628:16:17:89:425:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as lenders demand compensation for the expected increase indefaults.
3:92:5696:17:16:106:521:253:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In terms of forecasting macroeconomic conditions, the empirical success of this vein of
3:93:5783:16:16:89:521:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:research is considerable. Nevertheless, results vary substantially across different financial
3:94:5876:16:15:102:522:221:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:1The predictive content of various corporate credit spreads for economicactivity has been analyzed,
3:95:5975:15:11:89:521:206:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:among other, by Stock and Watson [1989]; Friedman and Kuttner [1998]; Duca [1999]; Emery [1999]; Gertler
3:96:6079:11:11:89:521:195:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and Lown [1999]; Ewing, Lynch, and Payne [2003]; Mody and Taylor [2004]; and Mueller [2007]. In addition,
3:97:6184:11:11:89:522:184:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Stock and Watson [2002b] have pointed out the ability of credit spreads to forecast economic growth using
3:98:6289:11:11:89:521:173:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:dynamic factor analysis, and King, Levin, and Perli [2007] find that corporate bond spread indexes contain
3:99:6395:11:11:89:522:162:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:important information about the near-term likelihood of a recession. In a related vein, an extensive empirical
3:100:6505:11:10:89:522:151:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:literature has emphasized the extent to which the slope of the yield curve—the so-called term spread—
3:101:6606:10:11:89:522:141:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:provides a signal for forecasting economic growth or for assessing the near-term risk of recession; see, for
3:102:6714:11:11:89:522:130:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:example, Dotsey [1998], Estrella and Hardouvelis [1991], Estrella and Mishkin [1998], and Hamilton and
3:103:6816:11:11:89:521:119:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Kim [2002]. More recent work on this topic includes Ang, Piazzesi, and Wei[2006] and Wright [2006]. A
3:104:6917:11:11:89:522:108:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:comprehensive review of the literature on the role of asset prices inforecasting macroeconomic outcomes is
3:105:7023:11:0:89:247:97:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:provided by Stock and Watson [2003a].
4:106:7061:0:17:90:522:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:instruments underlying the credit spreads under consideration as well as across different
4:107:7150:17:16:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:time periods. For example, the spread of yields between nonfinancial commercial paper and
4:108:7239:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:comparable-maturity Treasury bills—the so-called paper-bill spread—has lost much of its
4:109:7326:16:17:90:521:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecasting power since the early 1990s.2In contrast, yield spreads based on indexes of high-
4:110:7419:17:16:89:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:yield corporate bonds, which contain information from markets that were not in existence
4:111:7507:16:17:89:522:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:prior to the mid-1980s, have done particularly well at forecasting output growth during the
4:112:7598:17:16:89:521:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:previous decade, according to Gertler and Lown [1999] and Mody and Taylor [2004]. Stock
4:113:7685:16:33:89:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and Watson [2003b], however, find mixed evidence for the high-yield spread as a leading
4:114:7866:33:16:89:522:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:autumn of 1998. This dichotomy of findings is perhaps not surprising, because as financial
4:115:7956:16:17:89:521:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:markets evolve, the information content of specific financial assets prices may change as
4:116:8045:17:16:89:522:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:well. The fragility of results may also reflect the fact that this research has generally relied
4:117:8141:16:17:89:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on a single credit spread index, rather than on multiple indexes reflecting a broad cross-
4:118:8231:17:16:89:480:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:section—in terms of both default risk and maturity—of private debt instruments.
4:119:8310:16:17:106:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In addition to focusing on a single credit spread index, researchers often ignore the in-
4:120:8399:17:16:90:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:formation content of other asset prices when evaluating theforecasting ability of different
4:121:8490:16:16:90:521:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:default-risk indicators.  Although it is straightforward tocontrol for the general level of
4:122:8581:16:17:90:521:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equity prices in such analysis, it is usually not possible toobtain equity valuations of the
4:123:8673:17:16:90:521:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:borrowers whose debt securities are used to construct the credit spreads under considera-
4:124:8762:16:17:90:522:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tion.3Such information could potentially be used to distinguish movements in corporate
4:125:8848:17:16:90:521:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit spreads that are due to general trends in financial asset prices associated with a
4:126:8937:16:17:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:given class of borrowers from the movements in spreads that are specifically related to
4:127:9024:17:16:90:242:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:developments in credit markets.
4:128:9055:16:17:106:522:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:When assessing the information content of corporate creditspreads for economic activ-
4:129:9140:17:16:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ity, it is also important to control accurately for the maturity structure of the underlying
4:130:9232:16:16:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit instruments. The widely used paper-bill spreads, forexample, are based on short
4:131:9318:16:17:90:521:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity instruments—typically between one and six months—whereas the specific matu-
4:132:9402:17:16:90:521:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rity structure of corporate bond spread indexes such as the high-yield spread or Baa-Aaa
4:133:9490:16:17:90:521:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spread—though much longer—is not generally known. In general, short-term credit instru-
4:134:9577:17:16:90:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ments reflect near-term default risk, whereas longer-maturity instruments are likely better at
4:135:9671:16:17:90:521:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:capturing expectations about future economic conditions one to two years ahead, a forecast
4:136:9761:17:16:90:521:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:horizon typically associated with business cycle fluctuations. Thus, a correct assessment of
4:137:9853:16:16:90:522:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the ability of credit spreads to forecast at business cycle frequencies likely requires careful
4:138:9948:16:15:102:521:152:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:2Indeed, Thoma and Gray [1998] and Emery [1999] argue that the predictive content of the paper-bill
4:139:10047:15:7:90:232:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:spread may reflect one-time events.
4:140:10082:7:15:102:522:130:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:3Fama [1981], Harvey [1989], Stock and Watson [1989, 1999], and Estrella and Mishkin [1998] examine
4:141:10181:15:11:90:522:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the predictive content of various stock price indexes for economic activity and compare it to other financial
4:142:10290:11:0:90:202:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and nonfinancial indicators.
5:143:10319:0:17:90:476:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:attention to the maturity structure of securities used to construct credit spreads.
5:144:10402:17:16:106:521:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This paper considers credit spreads constructed directly from monthly data on prices of
5:145:10489:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:senior unsecured corporate debt traded in the secondary market over the 1990–2008 period,
5:146:10578:16:17:90:522:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:issued by about 900 U.S. nonfinancial corporations. In contrast to many other corporate
5:147:10665:17:16:90:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:financial instruments, long-term senior unsecured bonds represent a class of securities with
5:148:10757:16:17:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a long history containing a number of business cycles, an attribute that is most useful in the
5:149:10851:17:16:90:521:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:valuation process of debt instruments. In addition, the rapid pace of financial innovation
5:150:10941:16:33:90:522:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:over the past twenty years has not affected the basic structure of these securities. Thus,
5:151:11118:33:16:90:522:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bonds is likely to provide more consistent signals regarding economic outcomes relative to
5:152:11208:16:17:90:521:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads based on securities with a shorter history or securities whose structure or relevant
5:153:11300:17:16:90:346:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market has undergone a significant structural change.
5:154:11353:16:17:106:521:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We exploit the cross-sectional heterogeneity of our data by constructing an array of
5:155:11437:17:16:89:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit-spread portfolios sorted by the issuer’s ex-ante expected probability of default and
5:156:11528:16:17:89:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the bond’s remaining term-to-maturity. In the construction of these “bond portfolios,” we
5:157:11617:17:16:89:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rely on the monthly firm-specific expected default frequencies (EDFs) constructed by the
5:158:11705:16:16:89:522:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Moody’s/KMV corporation. Because they are based on observable information in equity
5:159:11788:16:17:89:522:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:markets, EDFs provide a more timely and potentially more objective assessment of credit
5:160:11875:17:16:89:522:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk compared with the issuer’s credit rating. Importantly, by building bond portfolios from
5:161:11967:16:17:89:522:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the “ground up,” we can also construct portfolios of stock returns—sorted by the same
5:162:12052:17:16:89:521:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit-risk categories—corresponding to the firms that issued those bonds. These matched
5:163:12140:16:17:89:521:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:portfolios of stock returns, in turn, serve as controls for news about firms’ future earnings
5:164:12233:17:16:89:437:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as these corporate borrowers experience shocks to their creditworthiness.
5:165:12306:16:17:106:521:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Two empirical methods are employed to assess the role of credit market factors in eco-
5:166:12392:17:16:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:nomic fluctuations. First, the analysis documents the predictive content of corporate bond
5:167:12482:16:16:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads in our credit-risk portfolios for measures of economic activity such as the growth
5:168:12572:16:17:90:522:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of nonfarm payroll employment and industrial production, and we compare the forecasting
5:169:12659:17:16:90:521:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:power of credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios to that of other default-risk indi-
5:170:12751:16:17:90:521:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cators emphasized in the literature. The results show that at shorter forecast horizons, the
5:171:12843:17:16:90:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:information content of credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios for these monthly
5:172:12931:16:17:90:521:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:measures of economic activity is comparable to that of standard credit spread indexes. At
5:173:13020:17:16:90:522:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:longer forecast horizons, however, our portfolios of credit spreads outperform—both in-
5:174:13107:16:16:90:521:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample and out-of-sample—standard default-risk indicators by almost a factor of two. The
5:175:13195:16:17:90:521:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:results from these forecasting exercises indicate that thepredictive power of corporate bond
5:176:13287:17:16:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads comes from the middle of the credit-quality spectrum, a result also documented by
5:177:13376:16:17:90:521:119:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Mueller [2007] who examines the predictive content of corporate bond spread indexes across
5:178:13466:17:0:90:522:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:different rating categories. Our results also indicate thatat longer forecasting horizons, the
6:179:13561:0:17:90:521:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:predictive power of corporate bond spreads is concentratedat long maturities. At these fore-
6:180:13653:17:16:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:casting horizons, the predictive content of publicly-available long maturity investment-grade
6:181:13746:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:corporate bond spread indexes—such as those rated between BBB and AA—is comparable
6:182:13828:16:17:90:521:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to that of our low-risk long maturity EDF portfolios. All told, these results imply that the
6:183:13920:17:16:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecasting ability of credit spreads is well captured by a single index that measures credit
6:184:14013:16:17:90:521:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads of long maturity bonds issued by firms with low to medium probability of default.
6:185:14102:17:16:106:522:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The second empirical approach assesses the impact on the macroeconomy of move-
6:186:14180:16:33:90:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ments in credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios within a structural factor-
6:187:14345:33:16:90:521:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:[2003], Bernanke, Boivin, and Eliasz [2005], and Stock and Watson [2005], an approach
6:188:14430:16:17:90:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:particularly well-suited to our case given the large number of variables under consideration.
6:189:14523:17:16:90:522:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Within the FAVAR framework, we identify credit market shocks from the corporate bond
6:190:14607:16:17:90:521:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads that are orthogonal to general measures of economicactivity, inflation, real interest
6:191:14700:17:16:90:521:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rates, and various financial indicators, as well as to equityreturns of firms whose outstand-
6:192:14793:16:17:90:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ing bonds were used to construct credit spreads in our EDF-based portfolios. According
6:193:14879:17:16:90:521:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to the results from our FAVAR analysis, an unanticipated worsening of business credit
6:194:14964:16:16:90:521:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:conditions—identified through the widening of corporate bond spreads that is orthogonal
6:195:15051:16:17:90:521:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to other contemporaneous information—predicts substantial and long-lasting declines in
6:196:15137:17:16:90:522:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:economic activity.  The decomposition of the forecast errorvariance implies that these
6:197:15223:16:17:90:521:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit market shocks account, on average, for more than 30 percent of the variation in
6:198:15309:17:16:90:521:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:economic activity (as measured by industrial production) at the two- to four-year horizon.
6:199:15399:16:17:90:521:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We also find that incorporating information from the stock market does not alter any of
6:200:15486:17:16:90:522:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:our conclusions. Thus to the extent that equity returns capture news about firms’ future
6:201:15574:16:17:90:522:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:earnings, our FAVAR specification identifies shocks to credit spreads that are orthogonal to
6:202:15666:17:16:90:521:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:such news and hence are specific to events that lead to disruptions in the corporate bond
6:203:15755:16:16:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market.4Overall, our results suggest that disturbances specific to credit markets account
6:204:15844:16:17:90:522:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for a substantial fraction of the volatility in U.S. economic activity during the 1990–2008
6:205:15935:17:16:90:123:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:period.
6:206:15942:16:17:106:522:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The remainder of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2discusses the characteristics
6:207:16032:17:16:89:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of our underlying security-level data, the construction of portfolios based on expected default
6:208:16127:16:17:89:522:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk, and presents the key summary statistics of and statistical relationships between our
6:209:16217:17:16:89:521:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:EDF-based financial indicators.  Section 3 presents our forecasting exercises.  Section 4
6:210:16306:16:16:89:380:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:contains results of our FAVAR analysis. Section 5 concludes.
6:211:16366:16:15:102:521:152:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:4By examining the joint behavior of stock prices and TFP, Beaudry and Portier [2006], identify a compo-
6:212:16469:15:11:89:522:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:nent in stock returns that captures news about future permanent changes in TFP; moreover, they show that
6:213:16573:11:11:89:521:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:movements in this component explains a significant portion of U.S. business cycle fluctuations. Jermann
6:214:16676:11:11:89:522:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and Quadrini [2007] develop a theoretical framework in which news about future technological opportunities
6:215:16782:11:11:89:521:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:raises firms’ current equity valuations, which relax credit constraints, thereby boosting current investment
6:216:16890:11:0:89:137:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and output.
7:217:16902:0:28:90:235:692:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:2  Data Description
7:218:16921:28:16:90:521:664:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The key information for our analysis comes from a large sample of fixed income securi-
7:219:17007:16:17:90:521:648:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ties issued by U.S. nonfinancial corporations.  Specifically, for a sample of 899 publicly-
7:220:17098:17:16:90:521:631:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:traded firms covered by the Center for Research in Security Prices (CRSP), month-end
7:221:17182:16:16:90:522:615:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:secondary market prices of their outstanding long-term corporate bonds were drawn from
7:222:17268:16:17:90:521:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the Lehman/Warga (LW) and Merrill Lynch (ML) databases. These two data sources in-
7:223:17350:17:16:90:522:582:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:clude secondary market prices for a significant fraction of dollar-denominated bonds publicly
7:224:17443:16:17:90:522:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:issued in the U.S. corporate cash market. The ML database is aproprietary data source of
7:225:17531:17:16:90:522:549:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:dailybond prices that starts in 1997. Focused on the most liquid securities in the secondary
7:226:17623:16:17:90:522:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market, bonds in the ML database must have a remaining term-to-maturity of at least two
7:227:17710:17:16:90:522:516:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:years, a fixed coupon schedule, and a minimum amount outstanding of $100 million for
7:228:17794:16:16:90:522:500:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:below investment-grade and $150 million for investment-grade issuers.  By contrast, the
7:229:17881:16:17:90:522:484:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:LW database ofmonth-endbond prices has a somewhat broader coverage and is available
7:230:17964:17:16:89:372:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from 1973 through mid-1998 (see Warga [1991] for details).
7:231:18022:16:17:106:522:451:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To ensure that the bonds yields used to construct portfoliosare obtained from com-
7:232:18104:17:16:89:521:434:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:parable securities, the analysis is restricted to senior unsecured issues only. For such se-
7:233:18196:16:17:89:522:418:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:curities with market prices in both the LW and LM databases, option-adjusted effective
7:234:18282:17:16:89:521:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:yields at month-end—a component of the bond’s yield that is not attributable to embedded
7:235:18370:16:17:89:522:385:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:options—are spliced across the two data sources. To calculate the credit spread at each
7:236:18457:17:16:89:522:368:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:point in time, the resulting yield oneachindividual security issued by the firm is matched
7:237:18547:16:16:89:521:352:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to the estimated yield on the Treasury coupon security of thesame maturity. The month-
7:238:18633:16:17:89:521:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:end Treasury coupon yields were taken from the daily estimates of the U.S. Treasury yield
7:239:18722:17:16:89:521:319:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:curve reported in G ̈urkaynak, Sack, and Wright [2006]. To mitigate the effect of outliers,
7:240:18813:16:17:89:522:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the analysis eliminates all observations with credit spreads smaller than 10 basis points and
7:241:18906:17:16:89:522:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with spreads greater than 5,000 basis points; in addition, eliminated were issues with a par
7:242:18998:16:17:89:521:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:value of less than $1 million, as such small issues are likelyplagued by significant liquidity
7:243:19092:17:16:89:521:253:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:concerns. These selection criteria yielded a sample of 5,045 individual securities, covering
7:244:19184:16:16:89:327:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the period from January 1990 to September 2008.
7:245:19231:16:17:106:521:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 1 contains summary statistics for the selected characteristics of bonds in our
7:246:19315:17:16:89:522:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample. Note that a typical firm has only a few senior unsecured issues outstanding at any
7:247:19405:16:17:89:521:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:point in time—the median firm, for example, has two such issues trading in the secondary
7:248:19493:17:16:89:522:171:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market at any given month. This distribution, however, exhibits a significant positive skew,
7:249:19585:16:17:89:521:155:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as the average firm has almost six different senior unsecured bond issues trading in the
7:250:19673:17:16:89:522:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market at a point in time. The distribution of the market values of these issues is similarly
7:251:19766:16:16:89:521:122:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:skewed, with the range running from $1.1 million to nearly $6.7 billion. Not surprisingly,
7:252:19856:16:0:89:522:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the maturity of these debt instruments is fairly long, with the average maturity at issue
8:253:19946:0:27:179:432:684:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 1: Summary Statistics of Bond Characteristics

8:267:20590:24:11:141:487:456:9:g_d0_f10:9:g_d0_f6:Note: Sample period: Monthly data from January 1990 to September 2008 for a
8:268:20665:11:11:125:486:445:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:sample of 899 nonfinancial firms. Sample statistics are based on trimmed data(see text
8:269:20751:11:7:125:171:434:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:for details).
8:270:20764:7:11:137:378:427:6:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f6:aMarket value of the outstanding issue deflated by the CPI.
8:271:20823:11:47:138:460:416:6:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f6:bMeasured relative to comparable maturity Treasury yield (see text for details).
8:272:20903:47:16:90:521:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of almost 14 years; the average term-to-maturity is about 11 years.  Because corporate
8:273:20989:16:17:90:522:353:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bonds typically generate significant cash flow in the form of regular coupon payments, the
8:274:21079:17:16:90:521:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effective duration is considerably shorter, averaging about 5.95 years over the sample period.
8:275:21173:16:16:90:522:320:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Although our sample spans the entire spectrum of credit quality—from “single D” to “triple
8:276:21263:16:17:90:522:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A”—the median bond/month observation, at BBB1, is still solidly in the investment-grade
8:277:21350:17:16:90:132:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:category.
8:278:21359:16:17:106:521:271:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The coupon rate on our sample of bonds averaged 7.60 percent during the sample period,
8:279:21445:17:16:89:521:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and the average total return, as measured by the nominal effective yield, was 7.46 percent
8:280:21535:16:17:89:522:238:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:per annum. Reflecting the wide range of credit quality, the distribution of yields is quite
8:281:21626:17:16:89:522:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wide, with the minimum of about 1.2 percent and the maximum ofmore than 57 percent.
8:282:21709:16:17:89:522:205:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Relative to Treasuries, an average bond in our sample generated a return of about 192 basis
8:283:21800:17:16:89:522:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:points above the comparable-maturity risk-free rate, with a standard deviation of 299 basis
8:284:21891:16:16:89:121:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:points.
8:285:21898:16:17:106:521:156:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A portion of observed credit spreads reflects compensation demanded by investors for
8:286:21982:17:16:90:522:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bearing the risk that a firm who issued the bonds will default on its payment obligations.
8:287:22072:16:17:90:521:123:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To measures this firm-specific likelihood of default at each point in time, we employ a
8:288:22159:17:16:90:521:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:monthly indicator that is widely used by financial market participants—the “Expected
8:289:22243:16:0:90:522:90:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Default Frequency” (EDF). This measure of default risk is constructed and marketed by
9:290:22329:0:16:90:522:693:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the Moody’s/KMV Corporation (MKMV). It measures the probability of default over the
9:291:22412:16:17:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:subsequent twelve-month period. The theoretical underpinnings to these probabilities of
9:292:22499:17:16:90:522:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:default are provided by the seminal work of Merton [1973, 1974]. According to this option-
9:293:22589:16:16:90:522:644:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:theoretic approach, the probability that a firm will defaulton its debt obligations at any
9:294:22679:16:17:90:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:point in the future is determined by three major factors: themarket value of the firm’s
9:295:22766:17:16:90:521:611:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assets; asset volatility; the risk-free interest rate and the firm’s leverage.5These factors are
9:296:22862:16:25:89:484:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:combined into a single measure of default risk calleddistance to default, defined as
9:297:22946:25:23:196:202:570:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:[
9:298:22955:23:0:203:252:547:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to Default
9:299:22965:0:16:253:259:570:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:]
9:300:22966:16:0:262:270:554:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:=
9:301:22967:0:7:279:284:578:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:[
9:302:22968:7:0:285:338:571:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Mkt. Value
9:303:22987:0:12:340:345:578:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:]
9:304:22988:12:0:347:355:566:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:−
9:305:22989:0:7:358:363:578:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:[
9:306:22990:7:0:365:400:571:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Default
9:307:23002:0:23:401:406:578:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:]
9:308:23003:23:7:274:279:555:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:[
9:309:23004:7:9:281:334:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Mkt. Value
9:310:23014:9:0:286:329:539:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of Assets
9:311:23023:0:12:335:340:555:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:]
9:312:23024:12:0:343:351:543:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:×
9:313:23025:0:7:354:359:555:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:[
9:314:23026:7:9:369:395:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Asset
9:315:23031:9:0:360:404:539:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Volatility
9:316:23041:0:41:406:415:555:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f9:].
9:317:23043:41:16:106:521:514:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Because the market value of assets and the volatility of assets are not directly observable,
9:318:23135:16:17:89:522:498:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:they have to be computed in order to calculate the distance todefault. Assuming that the
9:319:23223:17:16:89:522:481:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:firm’s assets are traded, the market value of the firm’s equitycan be viewed as a call option
9:320:23316:16:17:89:522:465:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on the firm’s assets with the strike price equal to the currentbook value of the firm’s total
9:321:23409:17:16:89:522:448:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:debt.6Using this insight, MKMV “backs out” the market value and thevolatility of assets
9:322:23496:16:17:89:522:432:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from a proprietary variant of the Black-Scholes-Merton option-pricing model, employing the
9:323:23586:17:16:89:522:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:observed book value of liabilities and the market value of equity as inputs (see Crosbie and
9:324:23678:16:16:89:522:399:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Bohn [2003] for details). In the final step, MKMV transforms the distance to default into
9:325:23767:16:17:89:522:383:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:an expected probability of default—the so-called EDF—usingan empirical distribution of
9:326:23853:17:32:89:162:366:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:actual defaults.
9:327:23869:32:23:89:294:334:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.1  Default-Risk Based Portfolios
9:328:23903:23:17:89:521:311:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We summarize the information contained in bond spreads and excess equity returns for
9:329:23987:17:16:89:522:294:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:our sample of firms by constructing portfolios based on expected default risk.7These
9:330:24071:16:16:90:522:278:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:default-risk portfolios are constructed by sorting credit spreads and excess equity returns in
9:331:24165:16:15:102:521:262:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:5In the original work of Merton [1974], the default point is equal to the book value of liabilities. Later
9:332:24271:15:11:90:521:247:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:structural default models relax this assumptions and allow for endogenous capital structure as well as
9:333:24373:11:11:90:521:236:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:strategic default. In these models, both the default time and default boundary are determined endogenously
9:334:24479:11:11:90:522:225:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and depend on firm-specific as well as aggregate factors; the voluminous literature on structural default
9:335:24584:11:11:90:521:214:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:models is summarized by Duffie and Singleton [2003]. Recent theoretical work has examined the importance
9:336:24688:11:11:90:522:203:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:of aggregate risk and different specifications of investors’ preferencesfor generating default-risk premiums
9:337:24796:11:11:90:522:192:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and matching historical credit spreads; see, for example, Chen, Collin-Dufresne, and Goldstein [2008] and
9:338:24901:11:11:90:522:181:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Chen [2008]. Empirically, however, MKMV has found that most defaults occur when the market value of
9:339:25000:11:11:90:521:170:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the firm’s assets drops to the value equal to the sum of the firm’s current liabilities and one-half of long-term
9:340:25113:11:11:90:521:159:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:liabilities (i.e., Default Point = Current Liabilities + 0.5×Long-Term Liabilities), and the default point is
9:341:25222:11:7:90:181:148:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:calibrated accordingly.
9:342:25245:7:15:102:521:141:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:6The assumption that all of the firm’s assets are traded is clearly inappropriate in most cases. Neverthe-
9:343:25351:15:11:90:522:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:less, as shown by Ericsson and Reneby [2004], this approach is still validprovided that at least one of the
9:344:25458:11:7:90:248:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:firm’s securities (e.g., equity) is traded.
9:345:25501:7:15:102:522:108:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:7Excess equity returns, which include dividends and capital gains, are measured relative to the yield on
9:346:25605:15:0:90:193:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:one-month Treasury bills.
10:347:25631:0:17:90:521:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:monthtinto five quintiles based on the distribution of EDFs in montht−1. To control for
10:348:25718:17:16:89:521:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity, we split each EDF-based quintile of credit spreadsinto four maturity categories:
10:349:25808:16:16:89:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(1)short maturity: credit spreads of bonds with the remaining term-to-maturityof less
10:350:25893:16:17:89:521:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:than (or equal) to 3 years; (2)intermediate maturity: credit spreads of bonds with the
10:351:25979:17:16:89:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:remaining term-to-maturity of more than 3 years but less than (or equal) 7 years; (3)long
10:352:26068:16:17:89:521:612:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:maturity: credit spreads of bonds with the remaining term-to-maturityof more than 7 years
10:353:26157:17:16:89:522:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:but less than (or equal) to 15 years; (4)very long maturity: credit spreads of bonds with
10:354:26246:16:33:89:522:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the remaining term-to-maturity of more than 15 years. We then compute an arithmetic
10:355:26413:33:16:89:522:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:average of excess equity returns in monthtfor each EDF portfolio. This procedure yields
10:356:26500:16:17:89:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:20 bond portfolios of credit spreads (five EDF quintiles and four maturity categories) and
10:357:26590:17:16:89:358:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:five EDF-based stock portfolios of excess equity returns.
10:358:26647:16:17:106:521:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 2 contains summary statistics of our variables by the five EDF quintiles. The
10:359:26730:17:16:89:521:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:average expected probability of default increases in a roughly linear fashion between the first
10:360:26825:16:17:89:521:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and the fourth quintiles before jumping sharply for firms in the fifth quintile. Consistent
10:361:26916:17:16:89:521:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the increase in the probability of default, both the average and the median credit
10:362:27003:16:16:89:521:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spread increase monotonically across the five EDF quintilesin all four maturity categories.
10:363:27094:16:17:89:521:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The Sharpe ratio within each maturity category is fairly constant for the portfolio of bonds
10:364:27186:17:16:89:521:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the first three EDF quintiles. However, the Sharpe ratio drops markedly for portfolios
10:365:27275:16:17:89:304:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:containing bonds issued by the riskiest firms.
10:366:27321:17:16:106:522:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The bottom panel of Table 2 examines the time-series characteristics of monthly excess
10:367:27407:16:17:89:521:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equity returns of firms in our five credit-risk categories. Excess return increase monotoni-
10:368:27499:17:16:89:521:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cally across the first four EDF quintiles, but the Sharpe ratios associated with these four
10:369:27590:16:17:89:521:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:stock portfolios are essentially constant. By contrast, firms in the fifth EDF quintile reg-
10:370:27682:17:16:89:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:istered considerably lower returns relative to their less risky counterparts, with an average
10:371:27775:16:38:89:437:283:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:(monthly) excess return over the 1990–2008 period of only 0.24 percent.8
10:372:27847:38:27:89:386:245:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:3  Credit Spreads and Economic Activity
10:373:27886:27:17:89:521:218:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This section examines the predictive power of credit spreads in our EDF-based bond port-
10:374:27974:17:16:89:522:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:folios and compare their forecasting performance—both in-sample and out-of-sample—with
10:375:28060:16:16:89:521:185:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:several commonly used credit spread indexes.  LettingYtdenote a measure of economic
10:376:28143:16:15:102:521:169:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:8This paltry performance is especially stark when one considers the Sharpe ratio for this category of
10:377:28244:15:11:90:522:154:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:firms, which is considerably below that of the less risky portfolios.The finding is consistent with the distress
10:378:28356:11:11:90:521:143:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:risk anomaly documented by a large empirical literature that has used different measures of default risk;
10:379:28461:11:0:90:449:132:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:see, for example, Griffin and Lemmon [2002] and Campbell, Hilscher, and Szilagyi [2008].

12:453:31817:16:16:89:521:418:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:only the vector of standard credit spread indexesZ1t; (2) an alternative specification that
12:454:31908:16:17:89:521:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:includes only the vectorZ2t, elements of which correspond to credit spreads in the four
12:455:31995:17:16:89:521:385:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity categories of an EDF quintile; and (3) a specification that includes both the
12:456:32081:16:17:89:522:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:vector of standard credit spread indexesZ1tand the vector of spreads in a particular EDF
12:457:32169:17:16:89:522:352:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quintileZ2t. For each specification and a forecast horizon of 3 and 12 months, we estimate
12:458:32259:16:17:89:522:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equations 1 and 2 by OLS. To take into account serial correlation induced by overlapping
12:459:32347:17:16:89:522:319:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecast errors, the estimated covariance matrix is computed according to Newey and West
12:460:32435:16:16:89:372:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:[1987], with the “lag truncation” parameter equal toh+ 1.
12:461:32492:16:17:106:522:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The set of standard default-risk indicators—the vectorZ1t—consists of four credit spread
12:462:32580:17:16:89:522:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:indexes, all of which have been used extensively to forecastreal economic activity; see
12:463:32667:16:17:89:521:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:Stock and Watson [2003a] for a comprehensive review. Specifically, we consider: (1)paper-
12:464:32756:17:16:89:521:237:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:bill spread: the difference between the yield on one-month nonfinancial AA-rated commer-
12:465:32844:16:17:89:522:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:cial paper and the yield on the constant maturity one-month Treasury bill; (2)Aaa cor-
12:466:32930:17:16:89:521:204:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:porate bond spread: the difference between the yield on an index of seasoned long-term
12:467:33016:16:17:89:522:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Aaa-rated corporate bonds and the yield on the constant maturity ten-year Treasury note;
12:468:33104:17:16:89:522:171:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(3)Baa corporate bond spread: the difference between the yield on an index of seasoned
12:469:33190:16:16:89:522:155:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:long-term Baa-rated corporate bonds and the yield on the constant maturity ten-year Trea-
12:470:33279:16:15:102:521:139:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:9An alternative approach to the directh-step ahead prediction method specified in equations 1–2 would be
12:471:33383:15:11:90:521:124:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:to specify a VAR—or some other joint one-step ahead model for employment growth, industrial production,
12:472:33486:11:11:90:522:113:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and credit spreads—and then iterate this model forwardhperiods. If the one-period ahead joint model is
12:473:33588:11:11:90:522:102:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:correctly specified, iterated forecasts are more efficient, whereas the directh-step ahead forecasts are more
12:474:33697:11:0:90:437:91:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:robust to model misspecification; see Marcellino, Stock, and Watson [2006] for details.
13:475:33786:0:16:90:521:693:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sury note; and (4)high-yield corporate bond spread: the difference between the yield on an
13:476:33876:16:17:90:521:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:index of long-term speculative-grade corporate bonds and theyield on the constant maturity
13:477:33966:17:16:90:521:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ten-year Treasury note.10Note that by including a paper-bill spread with spreads on long-
13:478:34055:16:16:90:522:644:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:term corporate bonds, our set of standard credit spread indexes captures the information
13:479:34143:16:33:90:411:628:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:content of default-risk indicators at both short and long horizons.11
13:480:34212:33:23:89:392:595:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.1  In-Sample Predictive Power of Credit Spreads
13:481:34261:23:17:89:522:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This section examines the in-sample predictive power of various credit spreads for our two
13:482:34351:17:16:89:521:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:measures of economic activity. The upper panel of Table 3 contains the results of this exer-
13:483:34443:16:16:89:521:539:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cise for the short-run forecast horizon (3 months), whereas the lower panel contains results
13:484:34535:16:17:89:521:523:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for the long-run forecast horizon (12 months). In both cases,we reportp-values associated
13:485:34624:17:16:89:521:506:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the exclusion tests on the two sets of credit spreads along with the explanatory power
13:486:34715:16:17:89:521:490:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:of each forecasting equation as measured by the adjustedR2. As a benchmark, theMemo
13:487:34798:17:16:89:521:473:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:item in both panels contains the in-sample fit from the VAR specification that excludes all
13:488:34889:16:17:89:158:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit spreads.
13:489:34904:17:16:106:521:440:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:When forecasting employment growth, the inclusion of credit spreads leads only to a
13:490:34987:16:16:89:521:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:modest improvement in the in-sample fit at the 3-month forecasthorizon. As evidenced by
13:491:35074:16:17:89:522:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:thep-values reported in the upper panel of Table 3, both the standard credit spread indexes
13:492:35165:17:16:89:522:391:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and credit spreads in each EDF quintile are statistically significant predictors of employment
13:493:35259:16:17:89:521:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:growth three months ahead. Moreover, when both sets of credit spreads are included in
13:494:35344:17:16:89:521:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the forecasting VAR, they all tend to remain statistically significant. Nevertheless, adding
13:495:35436:16:17:89:522:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:either set of credit spreads to the VAR results only in a relatively modest improvement in the
13:496:35530:17:16:89:522:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:explanatory power of the equation for employment growth. For example, the specification
13:497:35617:16:16:89:522:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that excludes all credit spreads yields an adjustedR2of 69 percent, only about 9 percentage
13:498:35708:16:17:89:522:293:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:points below the adjustedR2from a specification that includes standard credit spread
13:499:35792:17:16:89:351:276:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:indexes and credit spreads in the second EDF quintile.
13:500:35846:16:17:106:522:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The inclusion of credit spreads in the equation for industrial production, in contrast,
13:501:35933:17:16:89:522:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:leads to a substantial increase in predictive accuracy at the 3-month forecast horizon. Ac-
13:502:36024:16:15:98:522:227:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:10Commercial paper rates are taken from the “Commercial Paper Rates and Outstanding” Federal Reserve
13:503:36124:15:10:90:522:212:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:statistical release.  The source of Treasury yields and yields on Aaa- andBaa-rated corporate bonds is
13:504:36226:10:11:90:522:202:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:“Selected Interest Rates” (H.15) Federal Reserve statistical release.  To construct the high-yield spread,
13:505:36332:11:11:90:522:191:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:we use the High-Yield Master II index, a commonly used benchmark index for long-term speculative-grade
13:506:36434:11:8:90:284:180:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:corporate bonds administered by Merrill Lynch.
13:507:36480:8:14:98:522:172:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:11Note that we construct our standard corporate bond spread indexes using the ten-year Treasury yield.
13:508:36582:14:11:90:521:158:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:As emphasized by Duffee [1998], the corporate-Treasury yield spreads canbe influenced significantly by
13:509:36684:11:11:90:521:147:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:time-varying prepayment risk premiums, reflecting the call provisions on corporate issues.  According to
13:510:36788:11:11:90:522:136:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Duca [1999], corporate bond spreads measured relative to the yield on Aaa-rated bonds are more reflective
13:511:36893:11:11:90:521:125:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:of default risk than those measured relative to comparable-maturity Treasuries, which makes the former
13:512:36995:11:11:90:521:114:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:spreads more correlated with economic downturns. For comparison, we computed the Baa and the high-
13:513:37093:11:0:90:427:103:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:yield bond spread relative to the Aaa yield, and our results were virtually identical.

15:550:38991:0:17:90:521:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cording to theMemoitem, lags of industrial production and employment growth explain

15:552:39167:16:16:90:522:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:By including standard credit spread indexes in the forecasting VAR, the adjustedR2in-
15:553:39252:16:17:89:521:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:creases to almost 30 percent. Specifications that include credit spreads in our EDF-based

15:555:39432:16:17:89:522:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample fit comes from specifications that include credit spreads in the lowest two quintiles
15:556:39524:17:16:89:324:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the EDF distribution (EDF-Q1 and EDF-Q2).
15:557:39568:16:33:106:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The lower panel of Table 3 examines the in-sample explanatorypower of credit spreads
15:558:39742:33:16:90:521:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for both measures of economic activity is considerable.  In the case of nonfarm payroll
15:559:39829:16:17:90:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:employment, for example, standard credit spread indexes explain 66 percent of the variation
15:560:39920:17:16:90:521:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the 12-month ahead growth rate, a significant increases in the goodness-of-fit relative to
15:561:40013:16:17:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the specification that relies only on lags of employment growth and lags of the growth rate
15:562:40104:17:16:90:521:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in industrial production. Credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios do even better.
15:563:40193:16:17:90:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The information content of our default-risk indicators for the growth of employment is
15:564:40279:17:16:90:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:highest for the second and third EDF quintiles (EDF-Q2 and EDF-Q3), with the average
15:565:40363:16:16:90:522:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads in these two quintiles yielding adjustedR2s of about 75 percent. Results are even
15:566:40452:16:17:90:521:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more striking in the case of industrial production, a measure of economic activity for which
15:567:40544:17:16:90:521:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the explanatory power of our portfolio credit spreads significantly exceeds that of standard
15:568:40636:16:17:90:521:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:default-risk indicators. Whereas standard credit spread indexes explain about 20 percent
15:569:40724:17:16:90:521:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the variation in the 12-month ahead growth of industrial production, credit spreads
15:570:40810:16:17:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:associated with the first three EDF quintiles (EDF-Q1–EDF-Q3)explain over 50 percent
15:571:40894:17:16:90:434:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the variation in the 12-month ahead growth rate of industrial output.
15:572:40966:16:17:106:521:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The results in Table 3 highlight the gains in in-sample predictive accuracy for employ-
15:573:41053:17:16:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ment and industrial output growth at longer forecast horizon obtained from conditioning
15:574:41140:16:16:90:521:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios. The results of these forecasting exer-
15:575:41230:16:17:90:521:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cises indicate that the information content of credit spreads is concentrated in the low to
15:576:41321:17:16:90:522:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:medium risk categories. As we show below, the predictive content of credit spreads is also
15:577:41411:16:17:90:522:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:concentrated at the long end of the maturity spectrum. This result is shown graphically in
15:578:41501:17:16:90:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Figure 1, where the two panels depict the actual 12-month ahead growth of employment
15:579:41585:16:17:90:522:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and industrial production along with their respective fitted values obtained from simple
15:580:41673:17:16:90:522:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:regressions of these two variables on the credit spreads in the very long maturity EDF-
15:581:41760:16:16:90:522:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Q2 portfolio—that is, the portfolio with the highest overall predictive content, according
15:582:41850:16:17:90:521:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to the results in Table 3.  Note that these fitted values are a simple renormalization of
15:583:41939:17:16:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the credit spread dated 12 months before the time period overwhich the growth in em-
15:584:42023:16:17:90:521:119:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ployment and industrial production was computed. Remarkably, this single credit spread
15:585:42109:17:0:90:521:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecasted employment growth throughout the 2001 recession and the subsequent recovery.

16:613:42945:42:17:90:522:235:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:It also accurately predicted the current slowdown in employment growth, which peaked in
16:614:43032:17:16:90:521:218:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:January 2006. As shown in the bottom panel of Figure 1, the ability of this long-horizon
16:615:43120:16:17:90:521:202:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:relatively low-risk credit spread to predict accurately future economic activity as measured
16:616:43212:17:32:90:460:185:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:by the 12-month ahead growth in industrial production is evenmore striking.
16:617:43287:32:23:90:419:153:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.2  Out-of-Sample Predictive Power of Credit Spreads
16:618:43340:23:17:90:522:130:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This section examines the predictive content of credit spreads for our two measures of eco-
16:619:43431:17:16:90:521:113:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:nomic activity using pseudo out-of-sample forecasts. Specifically, for each forecast horizon
16:620:43523:16:0:90:522:97:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:h, the forecasting VAR given in equations 1–2 is estimated using all available data through,
17:621:43617:0:16:90:521:693:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and including, November 1999. We then calculate the (annualized)h-month ahead growth
17:622:43701:16:17:89:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rates of nonfarm payroll employment and industrial production and the associated forecast
17:623:43790:17:16:89:521:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:errors. The forecast origin—that is, November 1999—is thenupdated with an additional
17:624:43874:16:16:89:522:644:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:month of data, the VAR parameters are re-estimated using thisnew larger observation
17:625:43957:16:17:89:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:window, and new forecasts are generated. This procedure is repeated through the end of
17:626:44043:17:16:89:522:611:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the sample, thereby generating a sequence of pseudo out-of-sample forecasts for the two
17:627:44130:16:17:89:234:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:measures of economic activity.
17:628:44160:17:33:106:521:578:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Tables 4 contains the results of this exercise.  To quantify the pseudo out-of-sample
17:629:44338:33:16:89:522:545:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mean squared forecast error in annualized percentage points (RMSFE) for each specification.
17:630:44429:16:16:89:521:529:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To compare the predictive accuracy of credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios with
17:631:44519:16:17:89:521:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that of standard default-risk indicators, we then compute the ratio of the mean squared
17:632:44606:17:16:89:521:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecast error (MSFE) of the VAR specification augmented with EDF-based credit spreads
17:633:44692:16:17:89:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the MSFE of the specification that includes only standard credit spread indexes;p-
17:634:44779:17:16:89:521:463:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:values of the Diebold and Mariano [1995] test of equal predictive accuracy indicate whether
17:635:44870:16:17:89:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the difference in predictive accuracy between these two non-nested models are statistically
17:636:44961:17:16:89:149:430:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:significant.12
17:637:44975:16:17:106:522:414:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In the case of employment growth, the VAR specifications thatinclude credit spreads
17:638:45058:17:16:89:522:397:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in our EDF-based bond portfolios yield lower MSFEs at short-run forecast horizons than
17:639:45144:16:16:89:521:381:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the specification augmented with standard credit spread indexes. At the 3-month forecast
17:640:45232:16:17:89:522:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:horizon, the out-of-sample forecasting performance of credit spreads in the first three EDF
17:641:45323:17:16:89:522:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quintiles (EDF-Q1–EDF-Q3) for employment growth exceeds that of standard credit spread
17:642:45409:16:17:89:521:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:indexes by 20 to 25 percent, and these improvements in predictive accuracy are statistically
17:643:45501:17:16:89:521:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant at the 10 to 15 percent level.  The out-of-sample forecasting performance of
17:644:45589:16:17:89:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios for the growth of industrial production also
17:645:45681:17:16:89:521:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:exceeds that of standard default-risk indicators at the 3-month forecast horizon, although
17:646:45771:16:16:89:522:266:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the differences in predictive accuracy are not statistically significant at conventional levels.
17:647:45867:16:17:106:521:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The gain in out-of-sample predictive accuracy at the 12-month forecast horizon is espe-
17:648:45954:17:16:89:521:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cially striking, a result consistent with the in-sample analysis of the previous section. The
17:649:46047:16:17:89:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:predictive content of our portfolio credit spreads is againconcentrated among firms in the
17:650:46137:17:16:89:521:200:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:first three quintiles of the EDF distribution (EDF-Q1–EDF-Q3), which yield reductions in
17:651:46225:16:17:89:522:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the MSFEs on the order of 60 percent relative to the specification that includes the standard
17:652:46318:17:16:89:522:167:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:set of credit spread indexes. Moreover, these improvementsin predictive accuract are also
17:653:46407:16:16:89:419:151:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:highly statistically significant according to the Diebold-Mariano test.
17:654:46478:16:20:106:519:135:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The results reported in Table 4 point to significant improvements in the out-of-sample
17:655:46564:20:15:98:521:115:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:12Because the data in our forecasting VAR specification are overlapping, the asymptotic (long-run) vari-
17:656:46668:15:10:90:521:100:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:ance of the loss differential used to construct the Diebold-MarianoS-statistic allows for serial correlation of
17:657:46779:10:0:90:122:90:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:orderh.

19:759:50957:17:0:106:521:94:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As indicated by the narrow shaded band, forecasts of employment and industrial output
20:760:51044:0:17:90:522:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:growth based on credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios track quite well year-over-
20:761:51135:17:16:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:year growth in the actual series in both recessionary and expansionary times. In addition,
20:762:51225:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the predictive accuracy obtained from using credit spreadsin our EDF-based portfolios does
20:763:51315:16:17:90:522:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:not seem to reflect any “one-time” event or a specific subperiod. Importantly, our EDF-
20:764:51402:17:16:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:based forecasts capture the slowdown in economic activity associated with the 2001 recession
20:765:51494:16:17:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as well as the subsequent recovery. These EDF-based forecasts also predict the slowdown
20:766:51581:17:16:90:497:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in economic activity that has emerged since late 2006 with a high degree of accuracy.
20:767:51666:16:33:106:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In light of the ongoing turmoil in financial markets, investors and policymakers are ob-
20:768:51844:33:16:90:521:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for these two measures of economic activity through December 2009.13The average of the
20:769:51930:16:17:90:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:three EDF-based forecasts indicates that over the 12 months ending in December 2009, U.S.
20:770:52019:17:16:90:521:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:nonfarm payrolls will fall about 7.5 percent, while industrial production is projected to drop
20:771:52113:16:17:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:around 20 percent, declines that are four times greater thanthose experienced during the
20:772:52201:17:32:90:160:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2001 recession.
20:773:52216:32:23:90:367:448:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.3  Predicting an Index of Economic Activity
20:774:52261:23:17:90:521:425:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The previous results focused on forecasting the growth employment and industrial output.
20:775:52349:17:16:90:522:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In the FAVAR analysis below, real economic activity is summarized by a factor that relies,
20:776:52439:16:17:90:522:392:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in addition to the growth in employment and industrial production, on nine additional
20:777:52524:17:16:90:522:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:macroeconomic indicators that measure economic activity.Some of these series are leading
20:778:52612:16:17:90:522:359:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:indicators, or forward-looking variables such as new manufacturing orders, whereas other
20:779:52700:17:16:90:521:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:series such as unemployment are relatively sluggish. To assess the ability of credit spreads to
20:780:52795:16:16:90:522:326:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecast this broader set of economic indicators, we construct an index of economic activity,
20:781:52888:16:17:90:391:310:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:defined as the first principal component of these 11 time-series.
20:782:52953:17:16:106:521:293:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 5 reports both the in-sample and out-of-sample results obtained from univariate
20:783:53038:16:17:90:521:277:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forecasting specifications that include credit spread indexes along with the 12 monthly lags
20:784:53130:17:16:90:521:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the economic activity index. These results are very similar to those obtained using growth
20:785:53223:16:17:90:521:244:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in payroll employment and industrial production: Specifications that include credit spreads
20:786:53314:17:16:90:522:227:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the lowest three EDF quintiles provide modest improvements in out-of-sample forecasting
20:787:53404:16:16:90:521:211:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:performance at the 3-month horizon, and quantitatively large and statistically significant
20:788:53494:16:17:90:415:195:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:gains—both in-sample and out-of-sample—at the 12-month horizon.
20:789:53557:17:16:106:522:178:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As a final exercise, we explore the extent to which the predictive content of credit
20:790:53641:16:17:90:522:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads depends on the maturity structure of the underlyingsecurities. Because our credit
20:791:53730:17:16:90:522:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads rely on proprietary measures of default risk and issue-specific bond yields, we are
20:792:53821:16:25:90:521:129:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:also interested in determining whether ratings-based credit spreads yield similar forecasting
20:793:53914:25:15:98:522:104:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:13The year-over-year forecasts for December 2009 are based on the realized values of the two forecasting
20:794:54018:15:0:90:521:89:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:variables through December 2008, but we only use data through September 2008 to compute these forecasts.

23:876:58394:0:17:90:522:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:performance once one controls for maturity. These two issues are addressed by considering a
23:877:58485:17:16:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:simple in-sample forecasting exercise, in which the 12-monthchange in the index of economic
23:878:58576:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:activity is regressed on a 12-month lag of itself and a single credit spread index. We consider
23:879:58671:16:17:90:521:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:separately the credit spreads in our 20 bond portfolios as well as AA-rated and BBB-rated
23:880:58760:17:16:90:522:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit spreads for the same four maturity categories based on the Bloomberg Fair Value
23:881:58846:16:17:90:164:612:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:(BFV) model.14
23:882:58860:17:16:106:521:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The results of this exercise, which are reported in Table 6, again indicate that long
23:883:58945:16:13:89:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity low to medium risk credit spreads provide substantial gains in predictive content
23:884:59091:13:20:374:378:566:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:2
23:885:59122:20:16:89:521:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:12-month change in the economic activity index on the very long maturity credit spreads
23:886:59209:16:17:89:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the first three EDF quintiles (EDF-Q1–EDF-Q3) are about 65 percent, whereas those
23:887:59293:17:16:89:522:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that rely on short maturity credit spreads are below 25 percent. At shorter maturities, the
23:888:59384:16:17:89:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:information content of credit spreads in our EDF-based portfolios exceeds that of the AA-
23:889:59473:17:16:89:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and BBB-rated counterparts. At longer maturities, the information content of our EDF-
23:890:59558:16:17:89:521:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:based credit spreads is essentially the same as that of spreads in the two rating categories.
23:891:59651:17:16:89:521:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:These findings suggest that EDF-based measures of default risk provide timely information
23:892:59740:16:38:89:369:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that is especially useful for forecasting at shorter horizons.
23:893:59802:38:27:89:349:393:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4  Factor-Augmented VAR Analysis
23:894:59834:27:17:89:522:366:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This section examines the interaction between the credit spreads in our EDF-based bond
23:895:59920:17:16:89:521:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:portfolios and a wide range of measures of economic activityand inflation, the monetary
23:896:60007:16:17:89:521:333:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:policy rate, yields on Treasury securities of various maturities, excess returns on the matched
23:897:60102:17:16:89:521:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:EDF-based portfolios of stocks, and other financial indicators. We use the factor-augmented
23:898:60193:16:17:89:521:300:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:vector autoregression (FAVAR) methodology proposed by Bernanke and Boivin [2003] and
23:899:60277:17:16:89:522:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Bernanke, Boivin, and Eliasz [2005] to summarize a large number of macroeconomic and
23:900:60361:16:17:89:521:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:financial time series by a small number of unobservable (latent) factors. This methodology
23:901:60451:17:16:89:522:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is then used to identify shocks to corporate bond spreads andtrace out their dynamic effect
23:902:60542:16:16:89:196:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on the macroeconomy.
23:903:60562:16:15:98:521:218:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:14The BFV model provides daily estimates of the corporate bond yield curve utilizing prices of bonds
23:904:60662:15:11:90:522:203:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:with similar characteristics (i.e., currency, market type, industry, and credit rating). For comparability with
23:905:60773:11:11:90:522:192:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:our bond-level data, the sample is restricted to dollar-denominated bonds issued by industrial firms. For
23:906:60878:11:11:90:521:181:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:this segment of the corporate bond market, zero-coupon yields for AA- and BBB-rating categories at the
23:907:60980:11:10:90:521:170:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:maturities of 3-month, 6-month, 1-year, 2-year, 3-year, 4-year, 5-year, 7-year, 10-year, 15-year, 20-year, and
23:908:61090:10:11:90:522:160:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:30-year were obtained from the Bloomberg BFV data base. These two ratingcategories represent the highest
23:909:61194:11:11:90:522:149:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and lowest ratings for which spreads at all maturities are available since April 1991, the starting date of
23:910:61301:11:11:90:522:138:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the Bloomberg data. Credit spreads at all maturities are computed by utilizing daily Treasury yields of the
23:911:61408:11:11:90:521:127:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:same maturities, derived from the estimates of the zero-coupon Treasury yield curve (see G ̈urkaynak, Sack,
23:912:61515:11:11:90:522:116:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:and Wright [2006]). For each rating categories, we then constructed the samefour maturity categories as
23:913:61618:11:0:90:416:105:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:for our EDF-based portfolio and averaged the spreads in each maturity category.
24:914:61699:0:23:90:379:693:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:4.1  Specification, Identification, and Estimation
24:915:61749:23:17:90:521:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:LetXt,t= 1,2, . . . , T, denote a (n×1) vector of observations on all the variables in the
24:916:61839:17:16:89:522:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:FAVAR system in montht. We assume thatXtcan be partitioned asXt= [X′1tX′2t]′, where
24:917:61922:16:17:89:521:637:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:Xis the (n×1) vector whose elements correspond to measures of economicactivity and
24:918:62007:17:16:89:522:620:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:inflation, Treasury yields, excess equity returns, and other financial indicators, and elements
24:919:62102:16:16:89:522:604:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the (n2×1) vectorX2tcorrespond to credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios. We
24:920:62190:16:17:89:521:588:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assume that the information in the vector of observable variablesXtcan be summarized by a
24:921:62279:17:16:89:521:571:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:set of latent factors denoted by the (k×1) vectorFt, withk < n. The following assumption
24:922:62367:16:17:90:522:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are made with regards to this latent factor structure: A subset of factors—denoted by the
24:923:62456:17:16:90:521:538:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(k1×1) vectorF1t—spans all the information contained in the observed vectorXt, whereas
24:924:62542:16:17:89:522:522:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the remaining factors, denoted by the (k2×1) vectorF2t, are specific to credit spreads in
24:925:62631:17:16:89:350:505:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:our EDF-based portfolios—the so-called credit factors.
24:926:62685:16:17:106:521:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The relationship between the observed variables inXtand the latent factorsFt=
