24:969:63520:16:16:106:522:213:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To identify the vector of credit factorsF2t, we impose the following restrictions on
24:970:63604:16:17:90:522:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the system of equation 3 and 4.  First, we assume thatΛ12=0in equation 3.  This
24:971:63683:17:16:90:521:180:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:restriction on the factor loadings implies that once we haveconditioned on the factors
24:972:63769:16:16:90:522:164:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:inF1t, the remaining information content of credit spreads in ourEDF-based portfolios
24:973:63854:16:15:98:521:148:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:15Consistent with the assumptions underlying approximate factor models, the process for the vector of
24:974:63955:15:11:90:522:133:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:measurement errorsνtcan be weakly serially correlated and exhibit some degree of cross-sectional dependence
24:975:64062:11:11:89:522:122:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:(see, for example, Bai and Ng [2002]). Because the latent factors enter equation 3 without lags, the above
24:976:64168:11:11:89:522:111:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:specification corresponds to the static form of a dynamic factor model. However, as discussed by Stock and
24:977:64274:11:11:89:522:100:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Watson [2005], this is not a restrictive assumption, because the static factors can, in principle, contain an
24:978:64383:11:0:89:337:89:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:arbitrary number of lags of some underlying dynamic factors.
25:979:64445:0:17:90:522:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:has a systematic component specific to the corporate bond market that is reflected in
25:980:64530:17:16:90:521:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:its own factor structure.  Although the credit factors inF2thave no contemporaneous
25:981:64613:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect on the vectorX1t, they affect the factors inF1t—and, by extension, the vector of
25:982:64700:16:17:90:522:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:observed variablesX1t—with a lag through the dynamics of the VAR equation 4. The second
25:983:64787:17:16:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:identifying assumption is that the factors inF1tandF2tare orthogonal, an assumption that
25:984:64875:16:17:90:521:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:separates the residual information content from the corporate bond market from the factors
25:985:64965:17:16:90:274:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:summarizing the state of the economy.
25:986:65002:16:33:106:522:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A five-step estimation procedure that is computationally easy to implement and that
25:987:65179:33:16:90:522:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the (T×k1) matrix of factorsF1is estimated as the firstk1principle components of the
25:988:65263:16:17:90:521:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(T×n1) data matrixX1corresponding to the vector of variablesX1t. Second, each column
25:989:65347:17:16:90:522:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the (T×n2) data matrixX2corresponding to the vector of variables inX2t—that is,
25:990:65429:16:17:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit spreads associated with our EDF-based bond portfolios—is regressed on thek1factors
25:991:65518:17:16:90:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:inF1, witĥEdenoting the corresponding (T×n2) matrix of OLS residuals. Third, the
25:992:65599:16:17:90:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(T×k2) matrix of factorsF2is estimated as the firstk2principle components of the data
25:993:65684:17:16:90:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:matrix̂Efrom the second step. Fourth, factor loadings are estimatedby regressing each
25:994:65769:16:16:89:522:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:column of the (T×n) data matrixXon the estimated factorsF1andF2, imposing the
25:995:65846:16:17:89:522:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:restrictionΛ12=0. And fifth, the VAR(p) model in equation 4 is estimated by OLS using
25:996:65931:17:16:89:201:398:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:the estimated factors.16
25:997:65955:16:17:106:521:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Structural shocks affecting the vector of credit factorsF2tare identified using the
25:998:66038:17:16:89:522:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Cholesky decomposition ofΣ, the covariance matrix of the reduced-form VAR disturbances
25:999:66124:16:17:89:521:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in equation 4. In computing the Cholesky decomposition, thecredit factors are ordered last,
25:1000:66215:17:16:89:522:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and the individual components ofF2tare ordered in descending order with respect to their
25:1001:66303:16:17:89:522:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:associated eigenvalues. Thus identified “credit market shocks” correspond to unexpected
25:1002:66390:17:16:89:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:movements in corporate bond spreads that are contemporaneously uncorrelated with indi-
25:1003:66476:16:16:89:521:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cators of economic activity and inflation, interest rates, and other financial indicators as
25:1004:66568:16:17:89:283:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:summarized by the vector of factorsF1t.
25:1005:66607:17:16:106:522:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As noted above, the vectorX1tcontains a broad set of macroeconomic and financial
25:1006:66687:16:17:89:522:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:variables, whereas elements of the vectorX2tcorrespond to credit spreads in our EDF-
25:1007:66771:17:16:89:522:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:based bond portfolios.  The variables included inX1tcan be classified into five broad
25:1008:66856:16:17:89:522:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:categories: economic activity indicators, inflation indicators, risk-free interest rates, equity
25:1009:66952:17:16:89:522:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market indicators, and other financial indicators. In particular, the following 11 monthly
25:1010:67042:16:16:89:521:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:indicators of economic activity are included in our FAVAR specification: (1) the difference
25:1011:67133:16:17:89:522:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the civilian unemployment rate; (2) the log-difference of nonfarm payroll employment; (3)
25:1012:67225:17:15:98:521:135:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:16The latent factorsF1andF2are estimated using asymptotic principal components, the method whose
25:1013:67321:15:11:90:522:120:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:properties are discussed in detail by Stock and Watson [2002a] and Bai and Ng [2002]. Note that the residuals
25:1014:67430:11:11:90:521:109:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:from the second step, by construction, orthogonal toF1, implying that the estimated factorsF2are also
25:1015:67531:11:0:89:161:98:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:orthogonal toF1.
26:1016:67549:0:16:90:521:693:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the log-difference of industrial production index; (4) the difference in capacity utilization
26:1017:67642:16:17:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:index; (5) the log-difference of real durable goods orders; (6) the log-difference of real
26:1018:67732:17:16:90:521:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:nondurable good orders; (7) the Institute for Supply Management (ISM) diffusion index
26:1019:67817:16:16:90:521:644:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of activity in the manufacturing sector; (8) the log-difference of real personal consumption
26:1020:67909:16:17:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:expenditures (retail control category); (9) the log-difference of real disposable personal
26:1021:67999:17:16:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income; (10) the log-difference of housing starts; (11) and the log-difference of Conference
26:1022:68091:16:17:90:290:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Board’s leading economic indicator index.
26:1023:68132:17:33:106:521:578:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Price developments are summarized by the following six inflation indicators: (1) the
26:1024:68309:33:16:89:522:545:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the log-difference of the Producer Price index (PPI); (4) the log-difference of the core PPI;
26:1025:68402:16:16:89:521:529:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(5) the log-difference of the Journal of Commerce index of (spot) commodity prices; (6) the
26:1026:68493:16:17:89:522:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:log-difference of the price of oil as measured by price of a barrel of West Texas Intermediate
26:1027:68587:17:16:89:153:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(WTI) crude.
26:1028:68599:16:17:106:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Our FAVAR specification also includes the entire term structure of interest rates, starting
26:1029:68690:17:16:89:521:463:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:at the short end with the effective federal funds rate and continuing with the constant
26:1030:68777:16:17:89:522:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity Treasury yields at 6-month, 1-year, 2-year, 3-year, 5-year, and 10-year horizons,
26:1031:68867:17:16:89:521:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for a total of seven interest rates. Because nominal yields exhibit a discernible downward
26:1032:68957:16:17:89:522:414:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:trend over our sample period (1990–2008), they are converted into real terms to ensure their
26:1033:69049:17:16:89:218:397:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:approximate stationarity.17
26:1034:69076:16:16:106:522:381:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Developments in equity markets are summarized by the following eight series: (1) the
26:1035:69160:16:17:89:522:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:total value-weighted excess market return from CRSP; (2) theexcess equity returns of
26:1036:69244:17:16:89:522:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:firms in our five EDF-based stock portfolios; and (3) the Fama-French “SMB” and “HML”
26:1037:69329:16:17:89:521:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:factors to account for the different dynamics of equity returns in our EDF-based stock port-
26:1038:69421:17:16:89:521:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:folios. The final group of variables in the vectorX1t—six series—includes: (1) the implied
26:1039:69511:16:17:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:volatility on the S&P 500 index options (VIX) to capture uncertainty in the equity market;
26:1040:69601:17:16:90:522:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(2) the implied volatilities on Eurodollar and ten-year Treasury note futures, measures of
26:1041:69691:16:16:90:521:266:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:uncertainty associated with movements in short- and long-term interest rates, respectively;
26:1042:69782:16:17:90:522:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(3) the log-difference of the trade-weighted exchange value ofthe dollar against major cur-
26:1043:69873:17:15:98:522:233:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:17To do so, we utilize both the realized inflation and survey measures of inflation expectations reported
26:1044:69978:15:11:90:522:218:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:by the Survey of Professional Forecasters (SPF). Because the SPF is conducted at a quarterly frequency,
26:1045:70081:11:11:90:521:207:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:monthly estimates of inflation expectations are obtained from a linear interpolation of quarterly values.
26:1046:70186:11:11:90:521:196:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Specifically, the real federal funds rate is measured as the difference between the nominal rate and realized
26:1047:70295:11:11:90:522:185:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:inflation, where the realized inflation is given by the the differencebetween the log of the core CPI price
26:1048:70402:11:11:90:522:174:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:index and its lagged value 12 months earlier. The real 6-month Treasury yield is measured as the difference
26:1049:70509:11:10:90:522:163:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:between the nominal yield and the equally-weighted average of the realized inflation given above and the one-
26:1050:70618:10:11:90:522:153:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:year ahead expected CPI inflation as reported in the SPF. For the remaining Treasury yields, the expected
26:1051:70723:11:11:90:522:142:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:inflation at each specific horizon is constructed by calculating the appropriately weighted average of the one-
26:1052:70834:11:11:90:521:131:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:year ahead and the ten-year ahead expected CPI inflation reported in the SPF. For example, in calculating
26:1053:70939:11:11:90:522:120:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the 5-year real Treasury yield, we employ a simplifying assumptionthat the expected inflation over the next
26:1054:71046:11:11:90:521:109:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:five years is equal to an equally-weighted average of one-year ahead and ten-year ahead expected inflation
26:1055:71152:11:0:90:185:98:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:as reported in the SPF.
27:1056:71177:0:16:90:522:693:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rencies to control for the international dimension of the U.S. financial system; and (4) two
27:1057:71269:16:17:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:standard measures of liquidity—namely, the difference in the yields between the “off-the-
27:1058:71358:17:16:90:521:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:run” and “on-the-run” 10-year Treasury note and the difference between the 5-year swap
27:1059:71444:16:16:90:315:644:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rate and the yield on the 5-year Treasury note.
27:1060:71491:16:17:106:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Thus in our baseline specification, the vectorX1tcontains 38 monthly macroeconomic
27:1061:71573:17:16:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and financial time series, and the 20 elements of vectorX2tcorrespond to the average credit
27:1062:71664:16:17:90:522:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads in the 20 corporate bond portfolios classified by maturity and default risk. With
27:1063:71753:17:33:90:521:578:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this specification, our assumptions identify credit marketshocks that are orthogonal to the
27:1064:71929:33:16:90:521:545:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:based bond portfolios underlying the information content of the vectorX2t. Hence, the
27:1065:72014:16:16:90:522:529:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:FAVAR traces out the effect of a shock to corporate bond spreads that is unrelated to news
27:1066:72104:16:17:90:333:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:contained in stock returns of the same set of firms.
27:1067:72156:17:16:106:521:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The remaining question concerns the number of latent factors (k1andk2) and the order
27:1068:72240:16:17:90:521:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the VAR systemp.  In our baseline specification,k1= 4 andk2= 2.18Under this
27:1069:72318:17:16:90:522:463:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:parametrization, four common factors—denoted byF1t= [F11tF21tF31tF41t]′—are assumed
27:1070:72401:16:17:90:521:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to summarize the information contained in the vectorX1t, whereas the residual component
27:1071:72488:17:16:90:521:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of credit spreads in our EDF-based bond portfolios can be represented by two factors,
27:1072:72573:16:17:90:521:414:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:denoted byF2t= [F12tF22t]′. The order of the VAR system is set top= 6, a lag length
27:1073:72656:17:32:90:376:397:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:chosen according to the Akaike information criterion (AIC).
27:1074:72715:32:23:90:328:365:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:4.2  Shocks to Corporate Bond Spreads
27:1075:72752:23:17:90:521:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Before turning to our main results, we briefly discuss the estimates of the factorsF1t=
27:1076:72839:17:16:90:521:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:[F11tF21tF31tF41t]′and credit factorsF2t= [F11tF21t]′from the baseline specification. The first
27:1077:72934:16:16:90:522:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:four panels of Figure 3 depict the four factors associated with macroeconomic and financial
27:1078:73025:16:17:90:522:293:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:variables contained in the vectorX1t, and the bottom two panels show the estimates of the
27:1079:73114:17:16:90:521:276:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:two credit factors identified using the information from thecorporate bond market. (Tables
27:1080:73204:16:17:90:521:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:summarizing correlations between the six factors and all the variables inXtare shown in
27:1081:73291:17:16:90:155:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Appendix A.)
27:1082:73303:16:17:106:521:227:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:According to the correlations between the estimated factors and macroeconomic vari-
27:1083:73386:17:16:90:522:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ables, the first four factors shown in Figure 3 have a clear economic interpretation: Factor 1
27:1084:73480:16:14:98:521:194:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:18Recently, Bai and Ng [2002, 2007] and Stock and Watson [2005] have proposed several methods of how
27:1085:73580:14:11:90:522:180:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:to select formally the number of factors in such models. Because of the added complexity reflecting our
27:1086:73683:11:11:90:521:169:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:identification procedure, we adopted a more informal approach. Specifically, employing reasoning similar to
27:1087:73790:11:11:90:521:158:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:that of Forni, Giannone, Lippi, and Reichlin [2005] and Giannone, Reichlin, and Sala [2005],k1was chosen
27:1088:73894:11:11:89:521:147:9:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f18:by looking at the increase in the explained variation of the 38 macroeconomic and financial series inX1t
27:1089:73998:11:11:89:521:136:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:that resulted from increasing the number of factors inF1t. Given our choice ofk1, the number of credit
27:1090:74100:11:11:90:522:125:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:factorsk2was selected using the same approach. As a robustness check, we increased the number of factors
27:1091:74204:11:11:90:522:114:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:extracted from the data matrixX1from four to five, and to six, and we increased the number of factors
27:1092:74305:11:11:90:521:103:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:extracted from the data matrixX2to three. None of the resulting FAVAR specifications yielded materially
27:1093:74408:11:0:90:174:92:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:different conclusions.

29:1223:77408:17:16:90:522:108:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:deviation orthogonalized shock to the first credit factor.  (Impulse responses for all the
29:1224:77498:16:0:90:522:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:variables in our baseline specification, along with their respective 95-percent confidence
30:1225:77590:0:16:90:521:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intervals, are shown in Appendix B.19) This credit market shock widens corporate bond
30:1226:77675:16:16:90:521:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads across the entire spectrum of credit quality and across all maturities. The response
30:1227:77767:16:17:90:521:660:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of credit spreads associated with riskier bond portfolios is significantly greater than that of
30:1228:77862:17:16:90:522:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the less risky portfolios and is also more persistent. Furthermore, the jump in the riskiest
30:1229:77954:16:17:90:522:627:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:corporate bond spreads is somewhat more pronounced at the short end of the maturity
30:1230:78037:17:16:90:137:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spectrum.
30:1231:78046:16:17:106:521:594:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The impact of this credit shock on selected macroeconomic variables is shown in Fig-
30:1232:78130:17:16:89:521:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ure 5. A shock to the first credit factor is clearly contractionary, as evidenced by the fact
30:1233:78223:16:17:89:522:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that industrial production declines about 1 percentage points over a 24-month period.20In
30:1234:78312:17:16:89:522:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:addition to being statistically significant, the cumulative contraction in industrial output
30:1235:78404:16:16:89:522:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in response to a credit shock is economically significant, especially given that the response
30:1236:78497:16:17:89:521:512:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of credit spreads is in the order of only 10-50 basis points formost of the credit-risk distri-
30:1237:78592:17:16:89:522:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bution. The increasing slack in resource utilization following a shock to the corporate bond
30:1238:78684:16:17:89:522:479:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market is associated with a modest decline in the level of core CPI prices. These macroe-
30:1239:78773:17:16:89:521:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:conomic developments, in turn, lead to a fall in the general level of real interest rates. In
30:1240:78866:16:17:89:522:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:particular, real short-term interest rates decline about 15basis points at the trough, but
30:1241:78956:17:16:89:521:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:longer-term real Treasury yields fall somewhat less along the path, implying a steepening of
30:1242:79048:16:16:89:519:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the real Treasury yield curve in response to the innovation in the corporate bond spreads.
30:1243:79138:16:17:106:521:397:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The contractionary effects of this credit market shock implies a cumulative decline in
30:1244:79224:17:16:89:522:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the excess stock market return of about 2 percentage points over the horizon shown. The
30:1245:79311:16:17:89:522:364:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cumulative excess equity returns of the least and the most risky firms also fall initially,
30:1246:79402:17:16:89:521:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:though the latter effect is statistically indistinguishable from zero.  The impact of this
30:1247:79492:16:17:89:522:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:adverse credit market shock is also reflected in stock marketuncertainty, as the option-
30:1248:79580:17:16:89:521:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:implied volatility on the S&P 500 (VIX) increases notably inthe first six months after the
30:1249:79670:16:16:89:521:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shock. In summary, a shock to the first credit factor implies amodest increase in the overall
30:1250:79763:16:17:89:521:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:level of corporate bond spreads that leads to a sizable contraction in industrial output, a
30:1251:79854:17:18:89:519:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:deceleration in core prices, lower real interest rates and equity returns, and a rise in stock
30:1252:79948:18:15:98:521:247:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:19The confidence intervals of the impulse response functions are basedon a two-stage bootstrap procedure
30:1253:80052:15:11:90:521:232:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:that takes into account both the serial correlation and cross-sectional dependence of the measurement errors
30:1254:80160:11:11:90:521:221:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:in equation 3.  In particular, we first estimate the factors and factor loadings following the estimation
30:1255:80265:11:11:90:522:210:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:procedure described above. We then perform a sieve bootstrap on the residuals of the observation equation 3.
30:1256:80373:11:11:90:522:199:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:For each bootstrapped sample, we also re-estimate the factorsF1andF2, thereby taking into account that
30:1257:80475:11:11:90:521:188:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the factors appear as generated regressors in equation 4. Second, for each bootstrap loop of the observation
30:1258:80583:11:11:90:522:177:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:equation, we apply the “bootstrap-after-bootstrap” procedure of Kilian [1998] to the state-space equation 4
30:1259:80690:11:11:90:522:166:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:using the bootstrapped factors. This procedure is designed to takeinto account the small sample bias, the
30:1260:80795:11:11:90:521:155:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:lack of scale invariance, and the skewness of the distribution of the impulse response functions of the VAR
30:1261:80902:11:7:90:120:144:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:system.
30:1262:80909:7:15:98:522:137:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:20As discussed above, the macroeconomic and financial variables containedin the vectorX1twere, if
30:1263:81006:15:11:90:522:122:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:necessary, transformed using log or simple differencing to ensuretheir stationarity.  In such a case, we
30:1264:81110:11:11:90:522:111:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:cumulate their impulse responses to depict the impact of the credit market shock on levels of these variables;
30:1265:81220:11:10:90:521:100:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:similarly, we compute and show the cumulative responses of both the excess market return and the excess
30:1266:81323:10:0:90:286:90:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:equity returns of firms in the five EDF quintiles.

33:1645:85421:17:16:89:521:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more than 30 percent of the variation in the growth of industrial production at the two-
33:1646:85509:16:17:89:521:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to four-year forecast horizon. The shock to the first credit factor also explains a significant
33:1647:85604:17:16:89:521:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:fraction of the variation in both short- and long-term real interest rates and accounts for
33:1648:85695:16:16:89:521:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:30 percent of the forecast error variance in the excess equity returns. This credit market
33:1649:85785:16:17:89:522:512:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shock also accounts for a large fraction of the variation in corporate bond spreads but at a
33:1650:85877:17:16:89:522:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:higher frequency. Thus, variation in corporate bond spreads at the one- to two-year horizon
33:1651:85968:16:17:89:521:479:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:appears to explain a substantial fraction of the variation in both real activity and real in-
33:1652:86061:17:16:89:522:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:terest rates at the two- to four-year forecast horizon, a result consistent with the predictive
33:1653:86156:16:32:89:489:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:power for economic activity of corporate bond spread at long-run forecast horizons.
33:1654:86239:32:24:89:315:414:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:4.3  Shocks to Excess Equity Returns
33:1655:86275:24:16:89:522:390:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The baseline FAVAR specification analyzed the information content of corporate bond
33:1656:86358:16:17:89:522:374:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads that is orthogonal to both the aggregate stock market return and the average
33:1657:86442:17:16:89:521:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of excess returns of firms in our EDF-based stock portfolios. As a point of comparison,
33:1658:86529:16:17:89:521:341:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this section examines whether excess equity returns in our EDF-based stock portfolios also
33:1659:86619:17:16:89:522:324:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:contain information regarding economic activity that is not captured by either standard
33:1660:86706:16:16:89:395:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:macroeconomic indicators or the aggregate stock market return.
33:1661:86768:16:17:106:522:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To do so, we consider an alternative FAVAR specification thatrelies only on excess
33:1662:86850:17:16:89:522:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equity returns in our EDF-based stock portfolios to identifya shock to financial markets.
33:1663:86939:16:17:89:522:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Specifically, instead of the 20 credit spreads associated with our EDF-based bond portfolios,
33:1664:87032:17:16:89:521:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the elements of the vectorX2tin this alternative specification correspond to the (average)
33:1665:87122:16:17:90:521:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:excess equity returns in our five EDF-based stock portfolios.The elements of the vector
33:1666:87209:17:16:90:521:209:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:X1t, except for removing the excess equity returns in the five EDF-based portfolios, are left
33:1667:87302:16:16:90:521:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:unchanged.22This alternative FAVAR specification thus identifies shocksto firms’ earnings
33:1668:87391:16:17:90:521:177:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:contained in our EDF-based stock portfolios that are orthogonal to indicators of economic
33:1669:87480:17:16:90:497:160:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:activity and inflation, real interest rates, and aggregate stock market developments.23
33:1670:87567:16:15:98:521:144:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:21In contrast, the orthogonalized shock to the second credit factor has a statistically and economically
33:1671:87671:15:7:90:269:129:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:insignificant effect on real economic activity.
33:1672:87718:7:15:98:521:122:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:22The same identification scheme as in the baseline specification is employed to identify credit shocks; in
33:1673:87825:15:7:90:398:107:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:addition,k1= 4,k2= 2, andp= 6, exactly the same as in the baseline case.
33:1674:87897:7:0:98:522:100:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:23We have also considered a specification that that includes both the stock returns and the corporate bond

34:1703:89248:16:22:90:291:187:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:idiosyncratic news about earnings growth.

35:1839:90971:45:27:90:191:191:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:5  Conclusion
35:1840:90984:27:17:90:521:164:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Our results indicate that credit spreads on senior unsecured corporate debt have a sub-
35:1841:91071:17:16:90:522:147:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:stantial predictive power for future economic activity relative to that of previously used
35:1842:91161:16:17:90:521:131:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:default-risk indicators such as the paper-bill spread or the high-yield credit spread. This im-
35:1843:91256:17:16:90:521:114:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:provement in forecasting performance reflects the information content of spreads on longer-
35:1844:91347:16:0:90:522:98:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:maturity bonds issued by firms at the high-end and middle of thecredit-quality spectrum.
36:1845:91437:0:17:90:521:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:According to our FAVAR results, shocks to corporate bond spreads lead to quantitatively
36:1846:91524:17:16:90:521:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:large swings in economic activity and real interest rates. Such credit market shocks explain
36:1847:91616:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a sizable fraction of the variance in economic activity at the two- to four-year horizon.
36:1848:91705:16:17:90:522:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:These findings are consistent with the notion that an unexpected worsening of conditions
36:1849:91793:17:16:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in credit markets can cause a long-lasting economic downturnand that shocks to credit
36:1850:91878:16:17:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:markets have played an important role in business cycle fluctuations during the previous
36:1851:91966:17:16:90:177:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:decade and a half.
36:1852:91984:16:33:106:522:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The fact that credit market shocks generate such large effects may come as a bit of
36:1853:92156:33:16:89:522:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:prospects of firms than does the stock market. In that case, a shock to credit markets may
36:1854:92246:16:17:89:521:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:still reflect news regarding underlying cash flows rather than a disruption in the supply of
36:1855:92338:17:16:89:521:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit. But we are then left with the puzzle as to why stock prices do not incorporate all
36:1856:92428:16:17:89:522:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the relevant information about the firms’ profit opportunities? Although various theories
36:1857:92517:17:16:89:522:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of stock market behavior that emphasize departures from thestandard efficient markets
36:1858:92602:16:17:89:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:paradigm may help justify these findings, our results imply developments in corporate credit
36:1859:92694:17:16:89:519:447:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:markets provide important information regarding the future course of economic activity.24
36:1860:92783:16:16:106:521:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We offer two alternative explanations for our results. First, the recent empirical and
36:1861:92869:16:17:90:522:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:theoretical asset pricing literature has emphasized the inability of standard structural mod-
36:1862:92962:17:16:90:521:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:els of default to explain both the level and movements in credit spreads (see, for example,
36:1863:93053:16:17:90:521:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Martin [2001]). Accordingto this literature, a large part
36:1864:93142:17:16:90:522:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the variation in credit spreads is due to macroeconomic factors, particularly to liquidity
36:1865:93235:16:17:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and risk premiums. In the corporate bond market, the key investors are banks, insurance
36:1866:93322:17:16:90:521:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:companies, and other financial intermediaries.  To the extent that financial markets are
36:1867:93410:16:17:90:521:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:segmented, the risk attitude of the marginal corporate bondinvestor may reflect the will-
36:1868:93499:17:16:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ingness or ability of these institutions to bear risk. Thus,as conditions in the financial
36:1869:93589:16:16:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sector deteriorate, the premium on the risk of default rises, which causes a drop in invest-
36:1870:93681:16:17:90:522:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ment spending and a contraction in future economic activity, an argument consistent with
36:1871:93769:17:16:90:522:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the results of Philippon [2008] who finds that corporate bondspreads do particularly well
36:1872:93858:16:17:90:282:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:at forecasting business fixed investment.
36:1873:93899:17:16:106:521:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Second, the financial sector creates direct linkages between the banking sector and non-
36:1874:93987:16:17:90:521:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bank financial activity.  For example, the ability of nonfinancial corporations to finance
36:1875:94077:17:16:90:521:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:short-term liquidity needs by issuing commercial paper relies importantly on the ability of
36:1876:94168:16:16:90:521:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:these firms to obtain back-up lines of credit from banks. As monetary policy tightens, or
36:1877:94257:16:17:90:522:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:financial conditions in the banking sector deteriorate, banks may be forced to cut back on
36:1878:94347:17:16:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:their lines of credit. More generally, the process of creditdisintermediation may increase
36:1879:94437:16:15:98:521:119:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:24See Philippon [2008] for an overview of such theories and their potential implications for the information
36:1880:94545:15:0:90:230:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:content of stock and bond returns.
37:1881:94581:0:17:90:521:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:liquidity risk for nonfinancial firms, which, in the case of a severe deterioration in economic
37:1882:94676:17:16:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and financial conditions, may turn into insolvency risk.  Again, disturbances emanating
37:1883:94763:16:16:90:521:661:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from the financial sector would cause a rise in the cost of credit for nonfinancial firms. In
37:1884:94856:16:17:90:522:645:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:addition, to the extent that monetary policy shocks are not fully summarized by movements
37:1885:94945:17:16:90:521:628:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the Federal funds rate, these credit market disturbancesmay also reflect the anticipated
37:1886:95036:16:17:90:521:612:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tightening of monetary policy, which manifests itself in the disintermediation process sooner
37:1887:95129:17:16:90:521:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:than it is reflected in the observable movements in standard indicators of monetary policy.
37:1888:95220:16:33:90:521:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This alternative is consistent with the findings of Gertler and Lown [1999] and Mueller
37:1889:95392:33:16:90:385:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit market conditions over the course of the business cycle.
37:1890:95455:16:17:106:522:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As emphasized by Primiceri, Schaumburg, and Tambalotti [2006], there is strong empir-
37:1891:95540:17:16:90:521:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ical evidence supporting the notion that “intertemporal disturbances” are a major source
37:1892:95628:16:17:90:521:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of business cycle fluctuations. In dynamic stochastic general equilibrium models that allow
37:1893:95719:17:16:90:521:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for financial accelerator mechanisms, such as those developed by Kiyotaki and Moore [1997]
37:1894:95809:16:17:90:522:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and Bernanke, Gertler, and Gilchrist [1999], these disturbances may be linked directly to
37:1895:95898:17:16:90:521:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:changes in credit conditions. The rich amount of information contained in corporate bond
37:1896:95986:16:16:90:521:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spreads may be particularly useful for measuring and identifying the importance of these
37:1897:96074:16:17:90:522:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:financial mechanisms. To understand the inter-related effects of movements in risk premi-
37:1898:96163:17:16:90:521:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ums, changes in the health of financial institutions, and economic activity would require
37:1899:96252:16:17:90:521:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:extending these models to include financial market participants and changing risk attitudes
37:1900:96343:17:50:90:329:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in a fully-specified general equilibrium framework.
